height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Bronze_medal_icon_%28B_initial%29.svg/24px-Bronze_medal_icon_%28B_initial%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Bronze_medal_icon_%28B_initial%29.svg/32px-Bronze_medal_icon_%28B_initial%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="16" data-file-height="16" /></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"><span class="nowrap"> <a href="/wiki/1984_Amateur_World_Series" title="1984 Amateur World Series">1984 Cuba</a> </span></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"><a href="/wiki/United_States_national_baseball_team" title="United States national baseball team">Team</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Barry Lamar Bonds</b> (born July 24, 1964) is an American former <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">professional baseball</a> <a href="/wiki/Left_fielder" title="Left fielder">left fielder</a> who played 22 seasons in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) with the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-freeagent_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freeagent-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> He stands 6&#160;feet 2&#160;inches (1.88&#160;m) tall and weighs 228 pounds (103&#160;kg). Bonds received seven <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">NL</a> <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">MVP</a> awards and 14 <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star</a> selections, and is considered to be one of the greatest baseball players of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TNBJHBA-FBfaDI_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TNBJHBA-FBfaDI-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds was regarded as an exceptional <a href="/wiki/Hit_(baseball)" title="Hit (baseball)">hitter</a>: he led MLB in <a href="/wiki/On-base_plus_slugging" title="On-base plus slugging">on-base plus slugging</a> six times, and placed within the top five hitters in 12 of his 17 <a href="/wiki/Batting_average#Qualifications_for_the_batting_title" title="Batting average">qualifying</a> seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He holds many MLB hitting records, including most career <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home runs</a>, most home runs in a single season (73, set in 2001) and most career walks.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He also received eight <a href="/wiki/Rawlings_Gold_Glove_Award" title="Rawlings Gold Glove Award">Gold Gloves</a> for his defense in the <a href="/wiki/Outfield" title="Outfield">outfield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He is ranked second in career <a href="/wiki/Wins_Above_Replacement" title="Wins Above Replacement">Wins Above Replacement</a> among all major league <a href="/wiki/Position_player" title="Position player">position players</a> by both <a href="/wiki/Fangraphs" title="Fangraphs">Fangraphs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baseball-Reference.com" title="Baseball-Reference.com">Baseball-Reference.com</a>, behind only <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds led a controversial career, notably as a central figure in baseball\'s <a href="/wiki/Banned_substances_in_baseball_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Banned substances in baseball in the United States">steroids scandal</a>. In 2007, he was indicted on charges of <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obstruction_of_justice" title="Obstruction of justice">obstruction of justice</a> for allegedly lying to the grand jury during the federal government\'s investigation of <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Laboratory_Co-Operative" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay Area Laboratory Co-Operative">BALCO</a>. The perjury charges against Bonds were dropped and an initial obstruction of justice conviction<sup id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> was overturned in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Egelko_20150422_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Egelko_20150422-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2018, Bonds was not elected into the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">National Baseball Hall of Fame</a> in his sixth of 10 years of eligibility.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mlb.com_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mlb.com-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds served as the hitting coach for the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a> in 2016, and was fired at the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Early_life"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Early life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#College_career"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">College career</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Professional_career"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Professional career</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Draft_and_minor_leagues"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Draft and minor leagues</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Pittsburgh_Pirates_(1986\xe2\x80\x9392)"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Pittsburgh Pirates (1986\xe2\x80\x9392)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#San_Francisco_Giants_(1993\xe2\x80\x932007)"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">San Francisco Giants (1993\xe2\x80\x932007)</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-7"><a href="#1993_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">1993 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-8"><a href="#1994_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">1994 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-9"><a href="#1995_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.3</span> <span class="toctext">1995 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-10"><a href="#1996_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.4</span> <span class="toctext">1996 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11"><a href="#1997_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.5</span> <span class="toctext">1997 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-12"><a href="#1998_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.6</span> <span class="toctext">1998 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-13"><a href="#1999_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.7</span> <span class="toctext">1999 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-14"><a href="#2000_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.8</span> <span class="toctext">2000 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15"><a href="#2001_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.9</span> <span class="toctext">2001 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#2002_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.10</span> <span class="toctext">2002 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-17"><a href="#2002_postseason"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.11</span> <span class="toctext">2002 postseason</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18"><a href="#2003_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.12</span> <span class="toctext">2003 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#2004_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.13</span> <span class="toctext">2004 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#2005_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.14</span> <span class="toctext">2005 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21"><a href="#2006_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.15</span> <span class="toctext">2006 season</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#2007_season"><span class="tocnumber">3.3.16</span> <span class="toctext">2007 season</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Post-playing_career"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Post-playing career</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Public_persona"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Public persona</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Controversies"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Controversies</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#BALCO_scandal"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">BALCO scandal</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-27"><a href="#Perjury_case"><span class="tocnumber">6.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Perjury case</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Players&#39;_Union"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Players\' Union</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Game_of_Shadows"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Game of Shadows</i></span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Love_Me,_Hate_Me"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Love Me, Hate Me</i></span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Bonds_on_Bonds"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Bonds on Bonds</i></span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Career_distinctions"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Career distinctions</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Records_held"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Records held</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Records_shared"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Records shared</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Other_accomplishments"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Other accomplishments</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>\n<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Riverside,_California" title="Riverside, California">Riverside, California</a> to Patricia (n\xc3\xa9e Howard) and former major leaguer <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Bonds" title="Bobby Bonds">Bobby Bonds</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BBEB_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBEB-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Bonds grew up in <a href="/wiki/San_Carlos,_California" title="San Carlos, California">San Carlos</a> and attended <a href="/wiki/Jun%C3%ADpero_Serra_High_School_(San_Mateo,_California)" title="Jun\xc3\xadpero Serra High School (San Mateo, California)">Jun\xc3\xadpero Serra High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Mateo,_California" title="San Mateo, California">San Mateo</a>, where he excelled in <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>. He played on the <a href="/wiki/Junior_varsity_team" title="Junior varsity team">junior varsity team</a> during his freshman year and the remainder of his high school career on the <a href="/wiki/Varsity_team" title="Varsity team">varsity team</a>. He garnered a .467&#160;<a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a> his senior year, and was named prep <a href="/wiki/All-America" title="All-America">All-American</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The Giants drafted Bonds in the second round of the <a href="/wiki/1982_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="1982 Major League Baseball draft">1982 MLB draft</a> as a high school senior,<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> but the Giants and Bonds were unable to agree on contract terms when <a href="/wiki/Tom_Haller" title="Tom Haller">Tom Haller</a>\'s maximum offer was $70,000 ($177,510 today) and Bond\'s minimum to go pro was $75,000, so Bonds instead decided to attend college.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="College_career">College career</span></h2>\n<p>Bonds attended <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a>, hitting .347 with 45&#160;home runs and 175&#160;<a href="/wiki/Runs_batted_in" class="mw-redirect" title="Runs batted in">runs batted in</a> (RBI).<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1984 he batted .360 and had 30&#160;<a href="/wiki/Stolen_base" title="Stolen base">stolen bases</a>. In 1985, he hit 23&#160;home runs with 66&#160;RBIs and a .368&#160;batting average. He was a <a href="/wiki/Sporting_News" title="Sporting News">Sporting News</a> All-American selection that year. He tied the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> record with seven consecutive hits in the <a href="/wiki/College_World_Series" title="College World Series">College World Series</a> as sophomore and was named to All-Time College World Series Team in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Bonds was not well liked by his Sun Devil teammates, in part because in the words of longtime coach <a href="/wiki/Jim_Brock" title="Jim Brock">Jim Brock</a>, he was "rude, inconsiderate and self-centered." For instance, when he was suspended for breaking curfew, the other players initially voted against his return even though he was easily the best player on the team.<sup id="cite_ref-Stewart_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>He graduated from Arizona State in 1986 with a degree in <a href="/wiki/Criminology" title="Criminology">criminology</a>. He was named ASU On Deck Circle Most Valuable Player; other winners include <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Pedroia" title="Dustin Pedroia">Dustin Pedroia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Bloomquist" title="Willie Bloomquist">Willie Bloomquist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lo_Duca" title="Paul Lo Duca">Paul Lo Duca</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ike_Davis" title="Ike Davis">Ike Davis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> During college, he played part of one summer in the amateur <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Baseball_League" title="Alaska Baseball League">Alaska Baseball League</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Goldpanners" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaska Goldpanners">Alaska Goldpanners</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TAGoF_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TAGoF-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_career">Professional career</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Draft_and_minor_leagues">Draft and minor leagues</span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> drafted Bonds as the sixth overall pick of the <a href="/wiki/1985_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="1985 Major League Baseball draft">1985 Major League Baseball draft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  He joined the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_Nationals" title="Potomac Nationals">Prince William Pirates</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_League" title="Carolina League">Carolina League</a> and was named July 1985 Player of the Month for the league.<sup id="cite_ref-Pirates_Encyclopedia_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pirates_Encyclopedia-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 1986, he hit .311 in 44 games for the <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_Islanders" title="Hawaii Islanders">Hawaii Islanders</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_League" title="Pacific Coast League">Pacific Coast League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Pittsburgh_Pirates_.281986.E2.80.9392.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pittsburgh_Pirates_(1986\xe2\x80\x9392)">Pittsburgh Pirates (1986\xe2\x80\x9392)</span></h3>\n<p>Before Bonds made it to the major leagues in Pittsburgh, Pirate fan attendance was low, with 1984 and 1985 attendance below 10,000 per game for the 81-game home schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Bonds made his major league debut on May 30, 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In 1986, Bonds led <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) rookies with 16&#160;home runs, 48&#160;RBI, 36&#160;stolen bases and 65&#160;walks, but he finished 6th in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Year Award">Rookie of the Year</a> voting.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He played <a href="/wiki/Center_fielder" title="Center fielder">center field</a> in 1986, but switched to <a href="/wiki/Left_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Left field">left field</a> with the arrival of centerfielder <a href="/wiki/Andy_Van_Slyke" title="Andy Van Slyke">Andy Van Slyke</a> in 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-BWSBTD_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWSBTD-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In his early years, Bonds batted as the <a href="/wiki/Leadoff_hitter" title="Leadoff hitter">leadoff hitter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBHaPBBPP_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBHaPBBPP-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> With Van Slyke also in the outfield, the Pirates had a venerable defensive tandem that worked together to cover a lot of ground on the field although they were not close off the field.<sup id="cite_ref-BBHaPBBPP_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBHaPBBPP-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The Pirates experienced a surge in fan enthusiasm with Bonds on the team and set the club attendance record of 52,119 in the 1987 home opener.<sup id="cite_ref-BPTPSCR_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPTPSCR-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> That year, he hit 25&#160;home runs in his second season, along with 32&#160;stolen bases and 59&#160;RBIs.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds improved in 1988, hitting .283 with 24&#160;home runs.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  The Pirates broke the record set the previous year with 54,089 attending the home opener.<sup id="cite_ref-BPTPSCR_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BPTPSCR-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>  Bonds now fit into a highly respected lineup featuring <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Bonilla" title="Bobby Bonilla">Bobby Bonilla</a>, Van Slyke and <a href="/wiki/Jay_Bell" title="Jay Bell">Jay Bell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> He finished with 19&#160;homers, 58&#160;RBIs, and 14&#160;outfield <a href="/wiki/Assist_(baseball)" title="Assist (baseball)">assists</a> in 1989, which was second in the NL.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mlb89_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mlb89-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Following the season, rumors that he would be traded to the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> for <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Hamilton_(baseball)" title="Jeff Hamilton (baseball)">Jeff Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Wetteland" title="John Wetteland">John Wetteland</a>, but the team denied the rumors and no such trade occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-BWSBTD_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWSBTD-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds won his first <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">MVP Award</a> in 1990,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> hitting .301 with 33&#160;home runs and 114&#160;RBIs. He also stole 52 bases, which were third in the league, to become a first-time member of the <a href="/wiki/30%E2%80%9330_club" title="30\xe2\x80\x9330 club">30\xe2\x80\x9330 club</a>. He won his first <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Glove Award">Gold Glove Award</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silver_Slugger_Award" title="Silver Slugger Award">Silver Slugger Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> That year, the Pirates won the <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a> title for their first postseason berth since winning the <a href="/wiki/1979_World_Series" title="1979 World Series">1979 World Series</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cincinnati_Reds_seasons" title="List of Cincinnati Reds seasons">the Cincinnati Reds</a>, whose last post-season berth had also been in 1979 when they lost to the Pirates in <a href="/wiki/1979_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1979 National League Championship Series">that year\'s NLCS</a> defeated the Pirates in the <a href="/wiki/1990_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1990 National League Championship Series">NLCS</a> en route to winning the <a href="/wiki/1990_World_Series" title="1990 World Series">World Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1991, Bonds also put up great numbers, hitting 25 homers and driving in 116 runs, and obtained another Gold Glove and Silver Slugger. He finished second to <a href="/wiki/1991_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1991 Atlanta Braves season">the Atlanta Braves</a>\xe2\x80\x99 <a href="/wiki/Terry_Pendleton" title="Terry Pendleton">Terry Pendleton</a> (the NL batting champion) in the MVP voting.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The Pirates slugging outfield of Bonds, Bonilla and Van Slyke performed miserably in the 1990 and 1991 playoffs hitting .190 in 1990 (12 for 63) and .200 in 1991 (15 for 75).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 1992, Pirates general manager <a href="/wiki/Ted_Simmons" title="Ted Simmons">Ted Simmons</a> agreed to a deal with Atlanta Braves counterpart <a href="/wiki/John_Schuerholz" title="John Schuerholz">John Schuerholz</a> to trade Bonds, in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Pe%C3%B1a" title="Alejandro Pe\xc3\xb1a">Alejandro Pe\xc3\xb1a</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Mitchell_(baseball)" title="Keith Mitchell (baseball)">Keith Mitchell</a>, and a player to be named later. Pirates manager <a href="/wiki/Jim_Leyland" title="Jim Leyland">Jim Leyland</a> opposed the trade vehemently, and the proposal was rescinded.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Bonds stayed with Pittsburgh and won his second MVP award that season.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_20-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> While hitting .311 with 34 homers and 103 RBIs, he propelled the Pirates to their third straight <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">National League East</a> division title. However, Pittsburgh was defeated by the Braves in a seven-game <a href="/wiki/1992_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1992 National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a>. Bonds participated in the final play of <a href="/wiki/1992_National_League_Championship_Series_Game_7" class="mw-redirect" title="1992 National League Championship Series Game 7">Game 7</a> of the NLCS, whereby he fielded a base hit by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Cabrera_(baseball)" title="Francisco Cabrera (baseball)">Francisco Cabrera</a> and attempted to throw out <a href="/wiki/Sid_Bream" title="Sid Bream">Sid Bream</a> at home plate. But the throw to Pirates catcher <a href="/wiki/Mike_LaValliere" title="Mike LaValliere">Mike LaValliere</a> was late and Bream scored the winning run.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> For the third consecutive season, the NL East Champion Pirates were denied a trip to the World Series. Following the loss, Bonds and star teammate <a href="/wiki/Doug_Drabek" title="Doug Drabek">Doug Drabek</a> were expected to command salaries too high for Pittsburgh to again sign them.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds was never well-liked by reporters or fans while in Pittsburgh, despite winning two MVP awards. One paper even gave him an "award" as the "MDP" (Most Despised Pirate).<sup id="cite_ref-Stewart_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stewart-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="San_Francisco_Giants_.281993.E2.80.932007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="San_Francisco_Giants_(1993\xe2\x80\x932007)">San Francisco Giants (1993\xe2\x80\x932007)</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BarryBonds1993.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BarryBonds1993.jpg/220px-BarryBonds1993.jpg" width="220" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BarryBonds1993.jpg/330px-BarryBonds1993.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BarryBonds1993.jpg/440px-BarryBonds1993.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1014" data-file-height="1342" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BarryBonds1993.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonds in 1993</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1993_season">1993 season</span></h4>\n<p>In 1993, Bonds left the Pirates to sign a lucrative <a href="/wiki/Free_agent" title="Free agent">free agent</a> contract worth a then-record $43.75 million ($74.1 million today) over six years with the Giants, with whom his father had spent the first seven years of his career, and with whom his godfather <a href="/wiki/Willie_Mays" title="Willie Mays">Willie Mays</a> played 22 of his 24 Major League seasons. The deal was at that time the largest in baseball history, in terms of both total value and average annual salary.<sup id="cite_ref-43million_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43million-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Once he signed with the Giants, Bonds had intended to wear 24, his number during most of his stay with the Pirates, and after receiving Mays\' blessing the Giants were willing to unretire it until the public commotion from fans and media became too much.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> To honor his father, Bonds switched his jersey number to 25, as it had been Bobby\'s number in San Francisco.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds hit .336 in 1993, leading the league with 46 home runs and 123 RBI en route to his second consecutive MVP award,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and third overall. As good as the Giants were (winning 103 games), the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> won 104 in what some call the last great pennant race (because the <a href="/wiki/Wild_card_(sports)#Major_League_Baseball" title="Wild card (sports)">wild card</a> was instituted shortly thereafter).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1994_season">1994 season</span></h4>\n<p>In the lockout-shortened season of 1994, Bonds hit .312 with 37 home runs and a league-leading 74 walks,<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and he finished 4th in MVP voting.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1995_season">1995 season</span></h4>\n<p>In 1995, Bonds hit 33 homers and drove in 104 runs, hitting .294 but finished only 12th in MVP voting.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In 1994, he appeared in a small role as himself in the television film <i><a href="/wiki/Jane%27s_House" title="Jane&#39;s House">Jane\'s House</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/James_Woods" title="James Woods">James Woods</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anne_Archer" title="Anne Archer">Anne Archer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1996_season">1996 season</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrybonds1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Barrybonds1.JPG/220px-Barrybonds1.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Barrybonds1.JPG/330px-Barrybonds1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Barrybonds1.JPG/440px-Barrybonds1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrybonds1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonds on the field</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1996, Bonds became the first National League player and second (of the current list of four) major league player(s) to hit 40 home runs and steal 40 bases in the same season.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The other members of the <a href="/wiki/40%E2%80%9340_club" title="40\xe2\x80\x9340 club">40\xe2\x80\x9340 club</a> are <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Canseco" class="mw-redirect" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Canseco">Jos\xc3\xa9 Canseco</a>\xe2\x80\x931988, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a>\xe2\x80\x931998, and <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Soriano" title="Alfonso Soriano">Alfonso Soriano</a>\xe2\x80\x932006; his father Bobby Bonds was one home run short in 1973 when he hit 39 home runs and stole 43 bases.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds hit his 300th and 301st home runs off the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Marlins" class="mw-redirect" title="Florida Marlins">Florida Marlins</a>\' <a href="/wiki/John_Burkett" title="John Burkett">John Burkett</a> on April 27.<sup id="cite_ref-1Bbrih_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1Bbrih-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>  He became the fourth player in history to join the 300\xe2\x80\x93300 club with 300 stolen bases and 300 home runs for a career, joining <a href="/wiki/Willie_Mays" title="Willie Mays">Willie Mays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andre_Dawson" title="Andre Dawson">Andre Dawson</a>, and his father. Bonds\'s totals for the season included 129 runs driven in, a .308 average and a then-National League record 151 walks.<sup id="cite_ref-rage_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rage-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> He finished fifth in the MVP balloting.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1997_season">1997 season</span></h4>\n<p>In 1997, Bonds hit .291, his lowest average since 1989. He hit 40 home runs for the second straight year and drove in 101 runs, leading the league in walks again with 145.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He tied his father in 1997 for having the most 30/30 seasons, and he again placed fifth in the MVP balloting.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1998_season">1998 season</span></h4>\n<p>With two outs in the 9th inning of a game against the Arizona Diamondbacks on May 28, 1998, Bonds became only the fifth player in baseball history to be given an <a href="/wiki/Intentional_walk" class="mw-redirect" title="Intentional walk">intentional walk</a> with the bases loaded. <a href="/wiki/Nap_Lajoie" title="Nap Lajoie">Nap Lajoie</a> (1901), <a href="/wiki/Del_Bissonette" title="Del Bissonette">Del Bissonette</a> (1928) and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Nicholson_(baseball)" title="Bill Nicholson (baseball)">Bill Nicholson</a> (1944) were three others in the 20th century who received that rare honor. The first to receive one was <a href="/wiki/Abner_Dalrymple" title="Abner Dalrymple">Abner Dalrymple</a> in 1881.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> During a game against the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> on August 2, Bonds was hit by a pitch thrown by <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Bottalico" title="Ricky Bottalico">Ricky Bottalico</a>, leading to Bonds charging the mound and triggering a <a href="/wiki/Bench-clearing_brawl" title="Bench-clearing brawl">bench-clearing brawl</a>.\n</p><p>On August 23, Bonds hit his 400th career home run. By doing so, he became the first player ever to enter the 400\xe2\x80\x93400 club by having career totals of 400 home runs and 400 stolen bases; he is still the only player to have achieved this feat. The milestone home run came off <a href="/wiki/Kirt_Ojala" title="Kirt Ojala">Kirt Ojala</a>, who, like Burkett, was pitching for the Marlins.<sup id="cite_ref-1Bbrih_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1Bbrih-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> For the season, he hit .303 with 37 home runs and drove in 122 runs, winning his eighth Gold Glove,<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  He finished 8th in the MVP voting.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1999_season">1999 season</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BarryLamar_Bonds.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/BarryLamar_Bonds.jpg/220px-BarryLamar_Bonds.jpg" width="220" height="318" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/BarryLamar_Bonds.jpg/330px-BarryLamar_Bonds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0b/BarryLamar_Bonds.jpg 2x" data-file-width="347" data-file-height="502" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BarryLamar_Bonds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonds at the plate with the Giants</div></div></div>\n<p>1999 marked a career low up to that point for Bonds in terms of playing time. Bonds started off the 1999 season hitting well by batting .366 in the month of April with 4 home runs and 12 RBIs in the Giants first 12 games of the season. But on April 18 he was placed on the 15-day disabled list for only the 2nd time in his career up to that point. Bonds had suffered a torn tendon in his bicep as well as bone spurs in his elbow, both of which required surgery and cost him the rest of April and all of May. <sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Upon returning to action on June 9, Bonds struggled somewhat at the plate for the remainder of the 1999 season. A series of nagging injuries including elbow pain, knee inflammation and groin issues hampered his play. Only hitting .248 after his return from the disabled list, he still managed to slug 34 home runs, drive in 83 runs as well as hit for a .617 slugging percentage, despite missing nearly two full months with injuries and only playing in 102 games.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bill_James" title="Bill James">Bill James</a> ranked Bonds as the best player of the 1990s. He added that the decade\'s second-best player, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Biggio" title="Craig Biggio">Craig Biggio</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> had been closer in production to the decade\'s 10th-best player than to Bonds. In 1999, with statistics through 1997 being considered, Bonds ranked Number 34 on The Sporting News\' list of the 100 Greatest Baseball Players, making him the highest-ranking active player.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When the Sporting News list was redone in 2005, Bonds was ranked 6th behind Babe Ruth, Willie Mays, <a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Johnson" title="Walter Johnson">Walter Johnson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a>. Bonds was omitted from 1999\'s Major League Baseball All-Century Team, to which <a href="/wiki/Ken_Griffey,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Ken Griffey, Jr.">Ken Griffey, Jr.</a> was elected.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> James wrote of Bonds, "Certainly the most unappreciated superstar of my lifetime. ... Griffey has always been more popular, but Bonds has been a far, far greater player." In 1999, he rated Bonds as the 16th-best player of all time. "When people begin to take in all of his accomplishments", he predicted, "Bonds may well be rated among the five greatest players in the history of the game."<sup id="cite_ref-TNBJHBA-FBfaDI_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TNBJHBA-FBfaDI-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2000_season">2000 season</span></h4>\n<p>In 2000, the following year, Bonds hit .306 with career bests through that time in both slugging percentage (.688) and home runs (49) in just 143 games. He also drew a league-leading 117 walks.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2001_season">2001 season</span></h4>\n<p>The next year, Bonds\'s offensive production reached even higher levels, breaking not only his own personal records but several major league records. In the Giants\' first 50 games in 2001, he hit 28 home runs, including 17 in May\xe2\x80\x94a career high.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> This early stretch included his 500th home run hit on April 17 against <a href="/wiki/Terry_Adams_(baseball)" title="Terry Adams (baseball)">Terry Adams</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bh77haGge_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bh77haGge-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> He also hit 39 home runs by the All-star break (a major league record), drew a major league record 177 walks, and had a .515 on-base average, a feat not seen since Mickey Mantle and Ted Williams over forty years earlier. Bonds\'s slugging percentage was a major league record .863<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> (411 total bases in 476 at-bats), and, most impressively, he ended the season with a major league record 73 home runs.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 4, Bonds tied the previous record of 70 set by <a href="/wiki/Mark_McGwire" title="Mark McGwire">Mark McGwire</a> \xe2\x80\x93 which McGwire set in the 162nd game in 1998 \xe2\x80\x93 by homering off <a href="/wiki/Wilfredo_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Wilfredo Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Wilfredo Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> in the 159th game of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-2HRT_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2HRT-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> He then hit numbers 71 and 72 the following night off <a href="/wiki/Chan_Ho_Park" title="Chan Ho Park">Chan Ho Park</a>. Bonds added his 73rd off <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Springer" title="Dennis Springer">Dennis Springer</a> on October 7.<sup id="cite_ref-2HRT_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2HRT-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>  The ball was later sold to toy manufacturer Todd McFarlane for $450,000. He previously bought Mark McGwire\'s 70th home run ball from 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Bonds received the <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth_Home_Run_Award" title="Babe Ruth Home Run Award">Babe Ruth Home Run Award</a> for leading MLB in homers that season.<sup id="cite_ref-syken_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-syken-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2002_season">2002 season</span></h4>\n<p>Bonds re-signed with the Giants for a five-year, $90 million contract in January 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> He hit five home runs in the Giants\' first four games of the season, tying <a href="/wiki/Lou_Brock" title="Lou Brock">Lou Brock</a>\'s 35-year record for most home runs after four games. He won the NL batting title with a career-high .370 average and struck out only 47 times.<sup id="cite_ref-2002stats_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2002stats-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> He hit 46 home runs in 403 at-bats.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite playing in nine fewer games than the previous season, he drew 198 walks, a major-league record; 68 of them were intentional walks, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Willie_McCovey" title="Willie McCovey">Willie McCovey</a>\'s 45 in 1969 for another Major League record. He slugged .799, then the fourth-highest total all time. Bonds broke Ted Williams\' major league record for on-base average with .582. Bonds also hit his 600th home run, less than a year and a half after hitting his 500th.<sup id="cite_ref-2002stats_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2002stats-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>  The home run came on August 9 at home against <a href="/wiki/Kip_Wells" title="Kip Wells">Kip Wells</a> of the Pirates.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2002_postseason">2002 postseason</span></h4>\n<p>Bonds batted .322 with 8 home runs, 16 RBI, and 27 walks in the postseason en route to the <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series" title="2002 World Series">2002 World Series</a>, which the Giants lost 4\xe2\x80\x933 to the <a href="/wiki/Anaheim_Angels" class="mw-redirect" title="Anaheim Angels">Anaheim Angels</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2003_season">2003 season</span></h4>\n<p>In 2003, Bonds played in just 130 games. He hit 45 home runs in just 390 at-bats, along with a .341 batting average. He slugged .749, walked 148 times, and had an on-base average well over .500 (.529) for the third straight year.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He also became the only member of the career 500 home run/500 stolen base club by stealing second base on June 23 off of pitcher <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ric_Gagn%C3%A9" title="\xc3\x89ric Gagn\xc3\xa9">\xc3\x89ric Gagn\xc3\xa9</a> in the 11th inning of a tied ball game against the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> (against whom Bonds had tallied his 500th home run). Bonds scored the game-winning run later that inning.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2004_season">2004 season</span></h4>\n<p>In 2004, Bonds had perhaps his best season. He hit .362 en route to his second National League batting title, and broke his own record by walking 232 times. He slugged .812, which was fourth-highest of all time, and broke his on-base percentage record with a .609 average. Bonds passed Mays on the career home run list by hitting his 661st off of <a href="/wiki/Ben_Ford_(baseball)" title="Ben Ford (baseball)">Ben Ford</a> on April 13,<sup id="cite_ref-BhssisoF_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BhssisoF-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> He then hit his 700th off of <a href="/wiki/Jake_Peavy" title="Jake Peavy">Jake Peavy</a> on September 17.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Bonds hit 45 home runs in 373 at-bats, and struck out just 41 times, putting himself in elite company, as few major leaguers have ever had more home runs than strikeouts in a season. Bonds would win his fourth consecutive MVP award and his seventh overall.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> His seven MVP awards are four more than any other player in history. In addition, no other player from either league has been awarded the MVP four times in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> (The MVP award was first given in 1931). The 40-year-old Bonds also broke <a href="/wiki/Willie_Stargell" title="Willie Stargell">Willie Stargell</a>\'s 25-year record as the oldest player to win a Most Valuable Player Award (Stargell, at 39 years, 8 months, was National League co-MVP with <a href="/wiki/Keith_Hernandez" title="Keith Hernandez">Keith Hernandez</a> in 1979). On July 4, he tied and passed <a href="/wiki/Rickey_Henderson" title="Rickey Henderson">Rickey Henderson</a>\'s career bases on balls record with his 2190th and 2191st career walks.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As Bonds neared Aaron\'s record, Aaron was called on for his opinion of Bonds. He clarified that he was a fan and admirer of Bonds and avoided the controversy regarding whether the record should be denoted with an asterisk for Bonds\'s alleged steroid usage. He felt recognition and respect for the award was something to be determined by the fans.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> As the steroid controversy received greater media attention during the offseason before the 2005 season, Aaron expressed some reservations about the statements Bonds made on the issue. Aaron expressed that he felt drug and steroid use to boost athletic performance was inappropriate. Aaron was frustrated that the media could not focus on events that occurred in the field of play and wished drugs or gambling allegations such as those associated with <a href="/wiki/Pete_Rose" title="Pete Rose">Pete Rose</a> could be emphasized less.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, Aaron felt the whole steroid use issue was very controversial and decided that he would not attend any possible record-breaking games.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Aaron congratulated Bonds through the media including a video played on the scoreboard when Bonds eventually broke Aaron\'s record in August 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2005_season">2005 season</span></h4>\n<p>Bonds\'s salary for the 2005 season was $22 million, the second-highest salary in Major League Baseball (the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">Yankees</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a> earned the highest, $25.2 million).<sup id="cite_ref-BRSalaries_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BRSalaries-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\nBonds endured a knee injury, multiple surgeries, and rehabilitation. He was activated on September 12 and started in left field. In his return against the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a>, he nearly hit a home run in his first at-bat. Bonds finished the night 1-for-4.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Upon his return, Bonds resumed his high-caliber performance at the plate, hitting home runs in four consecutive games from September 18 to 21 and finishing with five homers in only 14 games.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2006_season">2006 season</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barry_Bonds3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Barry_Bonds3.jpg/220px-Barry_Bonds3.jpg" width="220" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Barry_Bonds3.jpg/330px-Barry_Bonds3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Barry_Bonds3.jpg/440px-Barry_Bonds3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="490" data-file-height="623" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barry_Bonds3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonds batting against the Chicago Cubs in 2006</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2006, Bonds earned $20 million (not including bonuses), the fourth highest salary in baseball. Through the 2006 season he had earned approximately $172 million during his then 21-year career, making him baseball\'s all-time highest paid player.<sup id="cite_ref-BRSalaries_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BRSalaries-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Bonds hit under .200 for his first 10 games of the season and did not hit a home run until April 22. This 10-game stretch was his longest home run slump since the 1998 season.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On May 7, Bonds drew within one home run of tying Babe Ruth for second place on the all-time list, hitting his 713th career home run into the second level of <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Bank_Park" title="Citizens Bank Park">Citizens Bank Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, off pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jon_Lieber" title="Jon Lieber">Jon Lieber</a> in a game in which the Giants lost to the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The towering home run\xe2\x80\x94one of the longest in Citizens Bank Park\'s two-season history, traveling an estimated 450&#160;feet (140&#160;m)\xe2\x80\x94hit off the facade of the third deck in right field.\n</p><p>On May 20, Bonds tied Ruth, hitting his 714th career home run to deep right field to lead off the top of the 2nd inning.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The home run came off left-handed pitcher <a href="/wiki/Brad_Halsey" title="Brad Halsey">Brad Halsey</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland A\'s</a>, in an <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague</a> game played in <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">Oakland, California</a>. Since this was an interleague game at an American League stadium, Bonds was batting as the <a href="/wiki/Designated_hitter" title="Designated hitter">designated hitter</a> in the lineup for the Giants. Bonds was quoted after the game as being "glad it\'s over with"<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and stated that more attention could be focused on <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a>, who was on a very rapid home run pace in early 2006.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:266px;max-width:266px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:127px;max-width:127px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Sign_counts_down_to_Barry_Bonds_713th_home_run.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Sign_counts_down_to_Barry_Bonds_713th_home_run.jpg/125px-Sign_counts_down_to_Barry_Bonds_713th_home_run.jpg" width="125" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Sign_counts_down_to_Barry_Bonds_713th_home_run.jpg/188px-Sign_counts_down_to_Barry_Bonds_713th_home_run.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Sign_counts_down_to_Barry_Bonds_713th_home_run.jpg/250px-Sign_counts_down_to_Barry_Bonds_713th_home_run.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2364" data-file-height="1891" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A sign counts up to Barry Bonds\'s 714th home run</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:135px;max-width:135px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:DSCN0163_Bonds715.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/DSCN0163_Bonds715.JPG/133px-DSCN0163_Bonds715.JPG" width="133" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/DSCN0163_Bonds715.JPG/200px-DSCN0163_Bonds715.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/DSCN0163_Bonds715.JPG/266px-DSCN0163_Bonds715.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Concession stand where home run number 715 was hit in center field</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>On May 28, Bonds passed Ruth, hitting his 715th career home run to center field off <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Byung-hyun_Kim" title="Byung-hyun Kim">Byung-hyun Kim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The ball was hit an estimated 445&#160;feet (140&#160;m) into center field where it went through the hands of several fans but then fell onto an elevated platform in center field. Then it rolled off the platform where Andrew Morbitzer, a 38-year-old San Francisco resident, caught the ball while he was in line at a concession stand.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Mysteriously, radio broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Dave_Flemming" title="Dave Flemming">Dave Flemming</a>\'s radio play-by-play of the home run went silent just as the ball was hit, apparently from a microphone failure. But the televised version, called by Giants broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Duane_Kuiper" title="Duane Kuiper">Duane Kuiper</a>, was not affected.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20060825_Barry_Bonds_follow_through.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/20060825_Barry_Bonds_follow_through.jpg/220px-20060825_Barry_Bonds_follow_through.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/20060825_Barry_Bonds_follow_through.jpg/330px-20060825_Barry_Bonds_follow_through.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/20060825_Barry_Bonds_follow_through.jpg/440px-20060825_Barry_Bonds_follow_through.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1930" data-file-height="1562" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20060825_Barry_Bonds_follow_through.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonds in August 2006 with the Giants</div></div></div>\n<p>On September 22, Bonds tied Henry Aaron\'s National League career home run record of 733. The home run came in the top of the 6th inning of a high-scoring game against the Milwaukee Brewers, at <a href="/wiki/Miller_Park_(Milwaukee)" class="mw-redirect" title="Miller Park (Milwaukee)">Miller Park</a> in Milwaukee, Wisconsin. The achievement was notable for its occurrence in the very city where Aaron began (with the Milwaukee Braves) and concluded (with the Brewers, then in the American League) his career. With the Giants trailing 10\xe2\x80\x938, Bonds hit a blast to deep center field on a 2\xe2\x80\x930 pitch off the Brewers\' <a href="/wiki/Chris_Spurling" title="Chris Spurling">Chris Spurling</a> with runners on first and second and one out. Though the Giants were at the time clinging to only a slim chance of making the playoffs, Bonds\'s home run provided the additional drama of giving the Giants an 11\xe2\x80\x9310 lead late in a critical game in the final days of a pennant race. The Brewers eventually won the game, 13\xe2\x80\x9312, though Bonds went 3 for 5, with 2 doubles, the record-tying home run, and 6 runs batted in.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 23, Bonds surpassed Aaron for the NL career home run record. Hit in Milwaukee like the previous one, this was a solo home run off <a href="/wiki/Chris_Capuano" title="Chris Capuano">Chris Capuano</a> of the Brewers.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> This was the last home run Bonds hit in 2006. In 2006, Bonds recorded his lowest <a href="/wiki/Slugging_percentage" title="Slugging percentage">slugging percentage</a> (a statistic that he has historically ranked among league leaders season after season) since 1991 with the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2007, the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News">New York Daily News</a></i> reported that Bonds had tested positive for <a href="/wiki/Amphetamine" title="Amphetamine">amphetamines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYP011107_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYP011107-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Under baseball\'s amphetamine policy, which had been in effect for one season, players testing positive were to submit to six additional tests and undergo treatment and counseling.<sup id="cite_ref-NYP011107_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYP011107-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The policy also stated that players were not to be identified for a first positive test, but the <i>New York Daily News</i> leaked the test\'s results.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> When the Players Association informed Bonds of the test results, he initially attributed it to a substance he had taken from the locker of Giants teammate <a href="/wiki/Mark_Sweeney" title="Mark Sweeney">Mark Sweeney</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NYP011107_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYP011107-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> but would later retract this claim and publicly apologize to Sweeney.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2007_season">2007 season</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrybonds2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Barrybonds2.JPG/220px-Barrybonds2.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Barrybonds2.JPG/330px-Barrybonds2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Barrybonds2.JPG/440px-Barrybonds2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrybonds2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonds at the plate against the Rockies in 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>On January 29, 2007, the Giants finalized a contract with Bonds for the 2007 season.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> After the commissioner\'s office rejected Bonds\'s one-year, $15.8 million deal because it contained a personal-appearance provision, the team sent revised documents to his agent, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Borris" title="Jeff Borris">Jeff Borris</a>, who stated that "At this time, Barry is not signing the new documents."<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Bonds signed a revised one-year, $15.8 million contract on February 15 and reported to the Giants\' Spring training camp on time.\n</p><p>Bonds resumed his march to the all-time record early in the 2007 season. After an opening game in which all he had was a first-inning single past third base against a right-shifted infield (immediately followed by a stolen base and then a base-running misjudgment that got him thrown out at home) and a deep out to left field late in the game,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Bonds returned the next day, April 4, with another mission. In his first at-bat of the season\'s second game at the Giants\' AT&amp;T Park, Bonds hit a <a href="/wiki/Chris_Young_(pitcher)" title="Chris Young (pitcher)">Chris Young</a> (of the San Diego Padres) pitch just over the wall to the left of straightaway center field for career home run 735.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> This home run put Bonds past the midway point between Ruth and Aaron.\n</p><p>Bonds did not homer again until April 13, when he hit two (736 and 737) in a 3 for 3 night that included 4 RBI against the Pittsburgh Pirates.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Bonds splashed a pitch by <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Franklin" title="Ryan Franklin">Ryan Franklin</a> into <a href="/wiki/McCovey_Cove" title="McCovey Cove">McCovey Cove</a> on April 18 for home run 738.<sup id="cite_ref-HR738_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HR738-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Home runs number 739 and 740 came in back to back games on April 21 and 22 against the Arizona Diamondbacks.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The hype surrounding Bonds\'s pursuit of the home run record escalated on May 14. On this day, Sports Auction for Heritage (a Dallas-based auction house) offered US$1 million to the fan who would catch Bonds\'s record-breaking 756th-career home run.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The million dollar offer was rescinded on June 11 out of concern of fan safety.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Home run 748 came on Father\'s Day, June 17, in the final game of a 3-game road series against the Boston Red Sox at <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a>, where Bonds had never previously played.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> With this homer, Fenway Park became the 36th major league ballpark in which Bonds had hit a home run. He hit a <a href="/wiki/Tim_Wakefield" title="Tim Wakefield">Tim Wakefield</a> knuckleball just over the low fence into the Giant\'s bullpen in right field. It was his first home run off his former Pittsburgh Pirate teammate, who became the 441st different pitcher to surrender a four-bagger to Bonds. The 750th career home run, hit on June 29, also came off a former teammate: <a href="/wiki/Liv%C3%A1n_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Liv\xc3\xa1n Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">Liv\xc3\xa1n Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The blast came in the 8th inning and at that point tied the game at 3\xe2\x80\x933.\n</p><p>On July 19, after a 21 at-bat hitless streak, Bonds hit 2 home runs, numbers 752 and 753, against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a>. He went 3\xe2\x80\x933 with 2 home runs, 6 RBIs, and a walk on that day.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The struggling last place Giants still lost the game, 9\xe2\x80\x938. On July 27, Bonds hit home run 754 against <a href="/wiki/Florida_Marlins" class="mw-redirect" title="Florida Marlins">Florida Marlins</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Rick_VandenHurk" class="mw-redirect" title="Rick VandenHurk">Rick VandenHurk</a>. Bonds was then walked his next 4 at-bats in the game, but a 2-run shot helped the Giants win the game 12\xe2\x80\x9310. It marked the first time since he had hit #747 that Bonds had homered in a game the Giants won.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> On August 4, Bonds hit a <span style="white-space:nowrap">382&#160;foot&#160;(116&#160;m)</span> home run against <a href="/wiki/Clay_Hensley" title="Clay Hensley">Clay Hensley</a> of the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> for home run number 755, tying Hank Aaron\'s all-time record.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN20070804_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN20070804-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Bonds greeted his son, Nikolai, with an extended bear hug after crossing home plate. Bonds greeted his teammates and then his wife, Liz Watson, and daughter Aisha Lynn behind the backstop. Hensley was the 445th different pitcher to give up a home run to Bonds.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN20070804_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN20070804-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Ironically, given the cloud of suspicion that surrounded Bonds, the tying home run was hit off a pitcher who had been suspended by baseball in 2005 for steroid use.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> He was walked in his next at bat and eventually scored on a fielder\'s choice.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>On August 7 at 8:51&#160;PM <a href="/wiki/Pacific_time_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific time zone">PDT</a>, at the Giants home AT&amp;T Park in San Francisco,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Bonds hit a <span style="white-space:nowrap">435&#160;foot&#160;(133&#160;m)</span> home run, his 756th, off a pitch from <a href="/wiki/Mike_Bacsik_(left-handed_pitcher)" title="Mike Bacsik (left-handed pitcher)">Mike Bacsik</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a>, breaking the all-time career home run record, formerly held by <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Coincidentally, Bacsik\'s father had faced Aaron (as a pitcher for the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a>) after Aaron had hit his 755th home run. On August 23, 1976, Michael J. Bacsik held Aaron to a single and a fly out to right field. The younger Bacsik commented later, "If my dad had been gracious enough to let Hank Aaron hit a home run, we both would have given up 756."<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> After hitting the home run, Bonds gave Bacsik an autographed bat.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The pitch, the seventh of the at-bat, was a 3\xe2\x80\x932 pitch which Bonds hit into the right-center field bleachers. The fan who ended up with the ball, 22-year-old Matt Murphy from <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> (and a <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">Mets fan</a>), was promptly protected and escorted away from the mayhem by a group of San Francisco police officers.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN.com_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN.com-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> After Bonds finished his home run trot, a ten-minute delay followed, including a brief video by Aaron congratulating Bonds on breaking the record Aaron had held for 33 years,<sup id="cite_ref-too_good_to_be_true_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-too_good_to_be_true-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and expressing the hope that "the achievement of this record will inspire others to chase their own dreams."<sup id="cite_ref-too_good_to_be_true_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-too_good_to_be_true-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Bonds made an impromptu emotional statement on the field, with Willie Mays, his godfather, at his side and thanked his teammates, family and his late father.<sup id="cite_ref-too_good_to_be_true_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-too_good_to_be_true-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Bonds sat out the rest of the game.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barry_Bonds_756_Ball.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Barry_Bonds_756_Ball.png/220px-Barry_Bonds_756_Ball.png" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Barry_Bonds_756_Ball.png/330px-Barry_Bonds_756_Ball.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Barry_Bonds_756_Ball.png/440px-Barry_Bonds_756_Ball.png 2x" data-file-width="1763" data-file-height="1371" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barry_Bonds_756_Ball.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonds\'s 756th home run ball in the Hall of Fame</div></div></div>\n<p>The commissioner, <a href="/wiki/Bud_Selig" title="Bud Selig">Bud Selig</a>, was not in attendance in this game but was represented by the Executive Vice President of Baseball Operations, <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Lee_Solomon" title="Jimmie Lee Solomon">Jimmie Lee Solomon</a>. Selig called Bonds later that night to congratulate him on breaking the record.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> also called Bonds the next day to congratulate him.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> On August 24, San Francisco honored and celebrated Bonds\'s career accomplishments and breaking the home run record with a large rally in <a href="/wiki/Justin_Herman_Plaza" title="Justin Herman Plaza">Justin Herman Plaza</a>. The rally included video messages from <a href="/wiki/Lou_Brock" title="Lou Brock">Lou Brock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Banks" title="Ernie Banks">Ernie Banks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ozzie_Smith" title="Ozzie Smith">Ozzie Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Montana" title="Joe Montana">Joe Montana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky" title="Wayne Gretzky">Wayne Gretzky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jordan" title="Michael Jordan">Michael Jordan</a>. Speeches were made by Willie Mays, Giants teammates <a href="/wiki/Omar_Vizquel" title="Omar Vizquel">Omar Vizquel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rich_Aurilia" title="Rich Aurilia">Rich Aurilia</a>, and Giants owner <a href="/wiki/Peter_Magowan" title="Peter Magowan">Peter Magowan</a>. Mayor <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Newsom" title="Gavin Newsom">Gavin Newsom</a> presented Bonds the key to the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">City and County of San Francisco</a> and Giants vice president Larry Baer gave Bonds the home plate he touched after hitting his 756th career home run.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The record-setting ball was consigned to an auction house on August 21.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Bidding began on August 28 and closed with a winning bid of US$752,467 on September 15 after a three phase <a href="/wiki/Online_auction" title="Online auction">online auction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The high bidder, <a href="/wiki/Fashion_designer" class="mw-redirect" title="Fashion designer">fashion designer</a> <a href="/wiki/Marc_Ecko" title="Marc Ecko">Marc Ecko</a>, created a website to let fans decide its fate.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Ben Padnos, who submitted the (US) $186,750 winning bid on Bonds\'s record-tying 755th home run ball also set up a website to let fans decide its fate.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Of Ecko\'s plans, Bonds said "He spent $750,000 on the ball and that\'s what he\'s doing with it? What he\'s doing is stupid."<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> 10 million voters helped Ecko decide to brand the ball with an asterisk and send it to the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Padnos sold 5-year ads on a website, www.endthedebate.com, where people voted by a two-to-one margin to smash the ball.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds concluded the 2007 season with a .276 batting average, 28 home runs, and 66 RBIs in 126 games and 340 at bats. At the age of 43, he led both leagues in walks with 132.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-playing_career">Post-playing career</span></h2>\n<p>On September 21, 2007, the San Francisco Giants confirmed that they would not re-sign Bonds for the 2008 season.<sup id="cite_ref-BwrwGf0tc_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BwrwGf0tc-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The story was first announced on Bonds\'s own web site earlier that day.<sup id="cite_ref-WdBBgfh_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WdBBgfh-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Bonds officially filed for <a href="/wiki/Free_agent" title="Free agent">free agency</a> on October 29, 2007.
