His agent <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Borris" title="Jeff Borris">Jeff Borris</a> said: "I\'m anticipating widespread interest from every Major League team."<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There was much speculation before the 2008 season about where Bonds might play.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> However, no one signed him during the 2008 or 2009 seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> If he had returned to Major League Baseball, Bonds would have been within close range of several significant hitting milestones: needing just 65 hits to reach 3,000, 4 runs batted in to reach 2,000, and 38 home runs to reach 800. He would have needed 69 more <a href="/wiki/Runs_scored" class="mw-redirect" title="Runs scored">runs scored</a> to move past <a href="/wiki/Rickey_Henderson" title="Rickey Henderson">Rickey Henderson</a> as the all-time runs champion, and 37 <a href="/wiki/Extra_base_hit" class="mw-redirect" title="Extra base hit">extra base hits</a> to move past <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a> as the all-time extra base hits champion.<sup id="cite_ref-BwrwGf0tc_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BwrwGf0tc-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of November 13, 2009, Borris maintained that Bonds was still not retired.<sup id="cite_ref-timbrown_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timbrown-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> On December 9, however, Borris told the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> that Bonds had played his last major league game.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Bonds announced on April 11, 2010, that he was proud of McGwire for admitting his use of steroids. Bonds said that it was not the time to retire, but he noted that he was not in shape to play immediately if an interested club called him.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>  In May 2015, Bonds filed a grievance against Major League Baseball through the players\' union arguing that the league colluded in not signing him after the 2007 season.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>  In August 2015, an arbitrator ruled in favor of MLB and against Bonds in his collusion case.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On December 15, 2011, Bonds was sentenced to 30 days of house arrest, two years of probation and 250 hours of community service, for an obstruction of justice conviction stemming from a grand jury appearance in 2003. However, U.S. District Judge <a href="/wiki/Susan_Illston" title="Susan Illston">Susan Illston</a> then delayed the sentence pending an appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 his conviction was upheld on appeal by a three judge panel of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBocu_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBocu-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> However, the full court later granted Bonds an <a href="/wiki/En_banc" title="En banc">en banc</a> rehearing, and on April 22, 2015, an 11-judge panel of the Ninth Circuit voted 10-1 to overturn his conviction.<sup id="cite_ref-Egelko_20150422_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Egelko_20150422-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On March 10, 2014, Bonds began a seven-day stint as a roving <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">spring training</a> instructor for the <a href="/wiki/2014_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="2014 San Francisco Giants season">Giants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>  On December 4, 2015, he was announced as the new hitting coach for the <a href="/wiki/2016_Miami_Marlins_season" title="2016 Miami Marlins season">Miami Marlins</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> but was <a href="/wiki/Dismissal_(employment)" title="Dismissal (employment)">relieved of his duties</a> on October 3, 2016, after just one season.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>  He followed up with a public thank-you letter, acknowledging <a href="/wiki/List_of_Miami_Marlins_owners_and_executives" title="List of Miami Marlins owners and executives">owner</a> <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Loria" title="Jeffrey Loria">Jeffrey Loria</a>, and the opportunity as "one of the most rewarding experiences of my baseball career."<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>  In 2017, Bonds officially rejoined the Giants organization as a special advisor to the CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>  On July 8, 2017, Bonds was added to the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants#San_Francisco_Giants_Wall_of_Famers" title="San Francisco Giants">Giants Wall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In his first six years of eligibility for induction to the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">National Baseball Hall of Fame</a>, Bonds received 36.2%, 34.7%, 36.8%, 44.3%, 53.8%, and 56.4% of the vote, all short of the 75% needed for induction.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mlb.com_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mlb.com-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 6, 2018, the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> announced their intentions to retire his number 25 jersey, which happened on August 11, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> His number 24 with the Pirates remains in circulation, most prominently worn by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Giles" title="Brian Giles">Brian Giles</a> from 1999 to 2003 and by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Alvarez_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro Alvarez (baseball)">Pedro Alvarez</a> from 2011 to 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_persona">Public persona</span></h2>\n<p>During his playing career, Bonds was frequently described as a difficult person, surly, standoffish and ungrateful. However, in one interview with <a href="/wiki/Terence_Moore" title="Terence Moore">Terence Moore</a> in 2016, he acknowledged regret over the persona which he had created. He attributed it to a response to the pressure he felt to perform as a young player with the Pirates. Remarked Bonds,<sup id="cite_ref-moore060116_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moore060116-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Hell, I kick myself now, because I\'m getting great press [since being more cooperative], and I could have had a trillion more endorsements, but that wasn\'t my driving force. The problem was, when I tried to give in a little bit, it never got better. I knew I was in the midst of that image, and I determined at that point that I was never going to get out of it.<sup id="cite_ref-moore060116_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moore060116-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>So I just said, \'I\'ve created this fire around me, and I\'m stuck in it, so I might as well live with the flames.\'<sup id="cite_ref-moore060116_166-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moore060116-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Bonds reports that for a short time during his playing days with the Giants he changed his demeanor at the behest of a group of teammates, resulting in him smiling much more frequently and engaging more with others with a pleasant attitude. Shortly thereafter, Bonds says, in the midst of a slump, the same group of teammates pleaded that he revert, having seemingly lost his competitive edge, and causing the team lose more. In spite of his protest that they would not appreciate the results, his teammates insisted. Bonds says he complied, maintaining that familiar standoffish edge the rest of his playing career.<sup id="cite_ref-moore060116_166-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moore060116-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="BALCO_scandal">BALCO scandal</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barry_bonds_mug_shot_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Barry_bonds_mug_shot_1.jpg/150px-Barry_bonds_mug_shot_1.jpg" width="150" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Barry_bonds_mug_shot_1.jpg/225px-Barry_bonds_mug_shot_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Barry_bonds_mug_shot_1.jpg/300px-Barry_bonds_mug_shot_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="469" data-file-height="595" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barry_bonds_mug_shot_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mug shot taken after 2007 indictment</div></div></div>\n<p>Since 2003, Bonds has been a key figure in the Bay Area Laboratory Co-operative (<a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Laboratory_Co-operative" title="Bay Area Laboratory Co-operative">BALCO</a>) scandal. BALCO marketed <a href="/wiki/Tetrahydrogestrinone" title="Tetrahydrogestrinone">tetrahydrogestrinone</a> ("the Clear"), a  performance-enhancing <a href="/wiki/Anabolic_steroid" title="Anabolic steroid">anabolic steroid</a> that was undetectable by doping tests.  He was under investigation by a federal <a href="/wiki/Grand_jury" title="Grand jury">grand jury</a> regarding his testimony in the BALCO case, and was indicted on <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obstruction_of_justice" title="Obstruction of justice">obstruction of justice</a> charges on November 15, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The indictment alleges that Bonds lied while under oath about his alleged use of steroids.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2003, Bonds first became embroiled in a scandal when <a href="/wiki/Greg_Anderson_(trainer)" title="Greg Anderson (trainer)">Greg Anderson</a> of the <a href="/wiki/BALCO" class="mw-redirect" title="BALCO">Bay Area Laboratory Co-operative</a> (BALCO), Bonds\'s trainer since 2000, was indicted by a federal <a href="/wiki/Grand_jury" title="Grand jury">grand jury</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Northern_District_of_California" title="United States District Court for the Northern District of California">United States District Court for the Northern District of California</a> and charged with supplying anabolic steroids to athletes, including a number of baseball players. This led to speculation that Bonds had used performance-enhancing drugs during a time when there was no mandatory testing in Major League Baseball. Bonds declared his innocence, attributing his changed physique and increased power to a strict regimen of bodybuilding, diet, and legitimate supplements.<sup id="cite_ref-Bttsdw_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bttsdw-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During grand jury testimony on December 4, 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-BlEg2yip_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BlEg2yip-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Bonds said that he used a clear substance and a cream that he received from his personal strength trainer, Greg Anderson, who told him they were the nutritional supplement flaxseed oil and a rubbing balm for arthritis.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> This testimony, as reported by <a href="/wiki/Lance_Williams_and_Mark_Fainaru-Wada" title="Lance Williams and Mark Fainaru-Wada">Lance Williams and Mark Fainaru-Wada</a>, has frequently been misrepresented. Later reports on Bonds\'s leaked grand-jury testimony contend that he admitted to unknowingly using "<a href="/wiki/The_cream" title="The cream">the cream</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Tetrahydrogestrinone" title="Tetrahydrogestrinone">the clear</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Bttsdw_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bttsdw-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2005, all four defendants in the BALCO steroid scandal trial, including Anderson, struck deals with federal prosecutors that did not require them to reveal names of athletes who may have used banned drugs.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Perjury_case">Perjury case</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Barry_Bonds_perjury_case" title="Barry Bonds perjury case">Barry Bonds perjury case</a></div>\n<p>On November 15, 2007, Bonds was indicted on four counts of <a href="/wiki/Perjury" title="Perjury">perjury</a> and one count of <a href="/wiki/Obstruction_of_justice" title="Obstruction of justice">obstruction of justice</a> as it relates to the government investigation of BALCO.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 14, 2008, a <a href="/wiki/Typo" class="mw-redirect" title="Typo">typo</a> in court papers filed by Federal prosecutors erroneously alleged that Bonds tested positive for steroids in November 2001, a month after hitting his record 73rd home run. The reference was meant instead to refer to a November 2000 test that had already been disclosed and previously reported.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The typo sparked a brief media frenzy.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>His trial for obstruction of justice was to have begun on March 2, 2009, but jury selection was postponed by 11th-hour appeals by the prosecution.<sup id="cite_ref-deny_appeal_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deny_appeal-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The trial commenced on March 21, 2011, in U. S. District Court, Northern District of California, with Judge Susan Illston presiding.<sup id="cite_ref-BBgMtd_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBgMtd-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> He was convicted on April 13, 2011, on the obstruction of justice charge, for giving an evasive answer to a question under oath.<sup id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> His sentence did not include prison. The conviction was initially upheld by a three judge panel of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit</a> in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-BBocu_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBocu-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> but a larger panel of the court voted 10-1 to overturn the conviction on April 22, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Egelko_20150422_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Egelko_20150422-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Players.27_Union"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Players\'_Union">Players\' Union</span></h3>\n<p>Bonds withdrew from the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Players_Association" title="Major League Baseball Players Association">MLB Players Association</a>\'s (MLBPA) <a href="/wiki/License" title="License">licensing</a> agreement because he felt independent marketing deals would be more lucrative for him. Bonds is the first player in the thirty-year history of the licensing program not to sign.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Because of this withdrawal, his name and likeness are not usable in any merchandise licensed by the MLBPA. In order to use his name or likeness, a company must deal directly with Bonds. For this reason he does not appear in some baseball <a href="/wiki/Video_games" class="mw-redirect" title="Video games">video games</a>, forcing game-makers to create generic athletes to replace him. For example, Bonds is replaced by "<a href="/wiki/Jon_Dowd" class="mw-redirect" title="Jon Dowd">Jon Dowd</a>" in <i><a href="/wiki/MVP_Baseball_2005" title="MVP Baseball 2005">MVP Baseball 2005</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_of_Shadows"><i>Game of Shadows</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Shadows" title="Game of Shadows">Game of Shadows</a></div>\n<p>In March 2006 the book <i><a href="/wiki/Game_of_Shadows" title="Game of Shadows">Game of Shadows</a></i>, written by <a href="/wiki/Lance_Williams_and_Mark_Fainaru-Wada" title="Lance Williams and Mark Fainaru-Wada">Lance Williams and Mark Fainaru-Wada</a>, was released amid a storm of media publicity including the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Initially small excerpts of the book were released by the authors in the issue of <i>Sports Illustrated</i>. The book alleges Bonds used <a href="/wiki/Stanozolol" title="Stanozolol">stanozolol</a> and a host of other steroids, and is perhaps most responsible for the change in public opinion regarding Bonds\'s steroid use.<sup id="cite_ref-TTABBaS_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTABBaS-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The book contained excerpts of grand jury testimony that is supposed to be sealed and confidential by law. The authors have been steadfast in their refusal to divulge their sources<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> and at one point faced jail time.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> On February 14, 2007, Troy Ellerman, one of <a href="/wiki/Victor_Conte" title="Victor Conte">Victor Conte</a>\'s lawyers, pleaded guilty to leaking grand jury testimony. Through the plea agreement, he will spend two and a half years in jail.<sup id="cite_ref-BlEg2yip_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BlEg2yip-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Love_Me.2C_Hate_Me"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Love_Me,_Hate_Me"><i>Love Me, Hate Me</i></span></h3>\n<p>In May 2006, former <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> writer <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Pearlman" title="Jeff Pearlman">Jeff Pearlman</a> released a revealing biography of Bonds entitled <i>Love Me, Hate Me: Barry Bonds and the Making of an Anti-Hero.</i> The book also contained many allegations against Bonds.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> The book, which describes Bonds as a polarizing insufferable braggart with a legendary ego and staggering ability, relied on over five hundred interviews, except with Bonds himself.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bonds_on_Bonds"><i>Bonds on Bonds</i></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bonds_on_Bonds" title="Bonds on Bonds">Bonds on Bonds</a></div>\n<p>In April 2006 and May 2006, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> aired a few episodes of a 10-part <a href="/wiki/Reality_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Reality TV">reality TV</a> (unscripted, <a href="/wiki/Documentary_film" title="Documentary film">documentary</a>-style) series starring Bonds.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The show, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Shows_on_ESPN#Original_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Shows on ESPN">Bonds on Bonds</a></i>, focused on Bonds\'s chase of <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a>\'s and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home run</a> records. Some felt the show should be put on hiatus until baseball investigated Bonds\'s steroid use allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> The series was canceled in June 2006, ESPN and producer Tollin/Robbins Productions citing "creative control" issues with Bonds and his representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>\n<p>Bonds met Susann ("Sun") Margreth Branco, the mother of his first two children (Nikolai and Shikari),<sup id="cite_ref-GAsdpa_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAsdpa-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> in August 1987. They eloped to <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> February 5, 1988. The couple separated in June 1994, divorced in December 1994, and had their marriage <a href="/wiki/Annulment" title="Annulment">annulled</a> in 1997 by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BaLBMP_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaLBMP-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The divorce was a media affair because Bonds had his Swedish spouse sign a <a href="/wiki/Prenuptial_agreement" title="Prenuptial agreement">prenuptial agreement</a> in which she "waived her right to a share of his present and future earnings" and which was upheld. Bonds had been providing his wife $20,000/month in child support and $10,000 in spousal support at the time of the ruling.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> During the hearings to set permanent support levels, allegations of abuse came from both parties.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The trial dragged on for months, but Bonds was awarded both houses and reduced support.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> On August 21, 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_California" title="Supreme Court of California">Supreme Court of California</a>, in an opinion signed by Chief Justice <a href="/wiki/Ronald_M._George" title="Ronald M. George">Ronald M. George</a>, unanimously held that "substantial evidence supports the determination of the trial court that the [prenuptial] agreement in the present case was entered into voluntarily."<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> In reaction to the decision, significant changes in California law relating to the validity and enforceability of premarital agreements soon followed.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, Bonds\'s son Nikolai, who served as a Giants <a href="/wiki/Batboy" title="Batboy">batboy</a> during his father\'s years playing in San Francisco and always sat next to his dad in the dugout during games,<sup id="cite_ref-batboyson_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batboyson-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> was charged with five <a href="/wiki/Misdemeanor" title="Misdemeanor">misdemeanors</a> resulting from a confrontation with his mother, Sun. Barry accompanied him to San Mateo County Superior Court.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the end of his first marriage, Bonds had an extensive intimate relationship with Kimberly Bell from 1994 through May 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Bonds purchased a home in <a href="/wiki/Scottsdale,_Arizona" title="Scottsdale, Arizona">Scottsdale, Arizona</a> for Kimberly.<sup id="cite_ref-BaLBMP_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaLBMP-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On January 10, 1998, Bonds married his second wife, Liz Watson, at the San Francisco <a href="/wiki/Ritz-Carlton" class="mw-redirect" title="Ritz-Carlton">Ritz-Carlton</a> Hotel in front of 240 guests.<sup id="cite_ref-BaLBMP_193-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaLBMP-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The couple lived in <a href="/wiki/Los_Altos_Hills,_California" title="Los Altos Hills, California">Los Altos Hills, California</a>, with their daughter Aisha<sup id="cite_ref-BaLBMP_193-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaLBMP-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SecondWife_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SecondWife-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> during their ten-and-a-half years of marriage before Watson filed for legal separation on June 9, 2009, citing <a href="/wiki/Irreconcilable_differences" title="Irreconcilable differences">irreconcilable differences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> On July 21, 2009, just six weeks later, Watson announced that she was withdrawing her Legal Separation action.<sup id="cite_ref-Reconciliation_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reconciliation-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> The couple were reconciled for seven months before Watson formally filed for divorce in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> on February 26, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-WatsonDivorce_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WatsonDivorce-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> On June 6, 2011, Bonds and Watson filed a legal agreement not to take the divorce to trial and instead settle it in an "uncontested manner", effectively agreeing to take the proceedings out of the public eye and end the marriage privately at an unspecified later date without further court involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-UncontestedManner_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UncontestedManner-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several of Bonds\'s family and extended family members have been involved in athletics as either a career or a notable pastime. Bonds has a younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Bonds,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Bobby Bonds, Jr.">Bobby, Jr.</a>, who was also a professional baseball player.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> His paternal aunt, <a href="/wiki/Rosie_Bonds" title="Rosie Bonds">Rosie Bonds</a>, is a former American record holder in the 80 meter <a href="/wiki/Hurdles" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurdles">hurdles</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> and competed in the 1964 Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> In addition, he is a distant cousin of Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBEB_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBEB-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Among Bonds\'s many real estate properties is a home he owns in the exclusive gated community of <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Beverly Park">Beverly Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Beverly Hills">Beverly Hills</a>, California.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An avid <a href="/wiki/Cyclist" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclist">cyclist</a>, Bonds chose the activity to be a primary means of keeping in shape and great passion since his playing career. Because knee surgeries, back surgeries, and hip surgeries made it much more difficult to run, cycling has allowed him to engage in sufficient cardiovascular activity to help keep in shape. As a result of the cycling, he has lost 25 pounds from his final playing weight of 240 pounds.<sup id="cite_ref-moore060116_166-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moore060116-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_distinctions">Career distinctions</span></h2>\n<table style="width: 100px; font-size: 90%; float:right; border: 2px solid #aaa; margin: 0em 1em 0em 0em;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/File:SFGiants_25.png" class="image"><img alt="SFGiants 25.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/SFGiants_25.png/95px-SFGiants_25.png" width="95" height="95" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/SFGiants_25.png/143px-SFGiants_25.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/SFGiants_25.png/190px-SFGiants_25.png 2x" data-file-width="560" data-file-height="560" /></a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align: center;">Barry Bonds\'s number 25 was <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_retired_numbers" title="List of Major League Baseball retired numbers">retired</a> by the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants#Retired_numbers" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> in 2018.\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Besides holding Major League career records in home runs (762), walks (2,558), and intentional walks (688), at the time of his retirement, Bonds also led all active players in RBI (1,996), <a href="/wiki/On-base_percentage" title="On-base percentage">on-base percentage</a> (.444), runs (2,227), games (2,986), extra-base hits (1,440), at-bats per home run (12.92), and <a href="/wiki/Total_bases" title="Total bases">total bases</a> (5,976). He is 2nd in doubles (601), slugging percentage (.607), stolen bases (514), at-bats (9,847), and hits (2,935), 6th in triples (77), 8th in sacrifice flies (91), and 9th in <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeouts</a> (1,539), through September 26, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-br-stats_21-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-br-stats-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bonds is the lone member of the 500\xe2\x80\x93500 club, which means he has hit at least 500 home runs (762) and stolen at least 500 bases (514); no other player has even 400 of both. He is also one of only four baseball players all-time to be in the 40\xe2\x80\x9340 club (1996), which means he hit 40 home runs (42) and stole 40 bases (40) in the same season; the other members are <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Canseco" class="mw-redirect" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Canseco">Jos\xc3\xa9 Canseco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Soriano" title="Alfonso Soriano">Alfonso Soriano</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_held">Records held</span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_sources" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section of a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Biographies_of_living_persons" title="Wikipedia:Biographies of living persons">biography of a living person</a> <b>needs additional <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">reliable sources</a>. 2004</li>\n<li>Intentional walks in a single season (120), 2004</li>\n<li>Consecutive games with a walk (18)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major 2001\xe2\x80\x9304</li>\n<li>National League <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Player_of_the_Month_Award" title="Major League Baseball Player of the Month Award">Player of the Month</a> selections player (age 38) to win the National League <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting title</a> (.370) for the first time, 2002</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" members of the 30\xe2\x80\x9330 club</li>\n<li>Home runs in a single post-season (8), 2002</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_accomplishments">Other accomplishments</span></h3>\n<table (1998, 2001\xe2\x80\x9304)</li>\n<li>3-Time NL Hank Aaron Award winner (2001\xe2\x80\x9302, 2004)</li>\n<li>Listed at #6 on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sporting_News" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sporting News">The Sporting News</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span> list of the 100 Greatest Baseball Players, the highest-ranked active player, in 2005.</li>\n<li>Named a finalist to the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Century_Team" title="Major League Baseball All-Century Team">Major League Baseball All-Century Team</a> in 1999, but not elected to the team in the fan balloting.</li>\n<li>Rating of 352 on Baseball-Reference.com\'s Hall of Fame monitor (100 is a good HOF candidate);<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> 9th among all hitters, highest among hitters not in HOF yet.</li>\n<li>Only the second player to twice have a single-season slugging percentage over .800, with his record .863 in 2001 and .812 in 2004. Babe Ruth was the other, with .847 in 1920 and .846 in 1921.</li>\n<li>Became the first player in history with more times on base (376) than official at-bats (373) in 2004. This was due to the record number of walks, which count as a time on base but not an at-bat. He had 135 hits, 232 walks, and 9 hit-by-pitches for the 376 number.</li>\n<li>With his father <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Bonds" title="Bobby Bonds">Bobby</a> (332, 461), leads all father-son combinations in combined home runs (1,094) and stolen bases (975), respectively through September 26, 2007.</li>\n<li>Played minor league baseball in both Alaska and Hawaii. In 1983, he played for the Alaska Goldpanners of Fairbanks in the Alaska Baseball League,<sup id="cite_ref-TAGoF_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TAGoF-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and in 1986, he played for the Hawaii Islanders in the Pacific Coast League.</li>\n<li>Featured on the cover of <a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> He has appeared as the main subject on the cover eight times in total; seven with the Giants and once with the Pirates. He has also appeared in an inset on the cover twice. He was the most recent Pirate player to appear on the cover,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> until Jason Grilli was featured in SIs edition of July 22, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div class="noprint metadata navbox" role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" style="font-weight:bold;padding:0.4em 2em"><ul style="margin:0.1em 0 0"><li style="display:inline"><span style="display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap"><span style="margin:0 0.5em"><a href="/wiki/File:P_vip.svg" class="image"><img alt="P vip.svg"
